class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice">\n    <!-- CentralNotice -->\n   </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Human mission to Mars\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       "Man on Mars" redirects here. For the song, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Man_on_Mars_(song)" title="Man on Mars (song)">\n        Man on Mars (song)\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="50" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/50px-Mergefrom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/75px-Mergefrom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/100px-Mergefrom.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          It has been suggested that\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Mars_race" title="Mars race">\n            Mars race\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          be\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Merging" title="Wikipedia:Merging">\n           merged\n          </a>\n          into this article. (\n          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Human_mission_to_Mars#Proposed_merge_with_Mars_race" title="Talk:Human mission to Mars">\n           Discuss\n          </a>\n          )\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            Proposed since April 2017.\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="60" height="17" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/50px-Split-arrows.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/75px-Split-arrows.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/100px-Split-arrows.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          It has been suggested that this article be\n          <b>\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Splitting" title="Wikipedia:Splitting">\n            split\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          into multiple articles. (\n          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Human_mission_to_Mars#Proposed_merge_with_Mars_race" title="Talk:Human mission to Mars">\n           Discuss\n          </a>\n          )\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (April 2017)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1600" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg/220px-Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg/330px-Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg/440px-Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astronaut_working_on_Mars.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rendition of person in a spacesuit on Mars\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        human mission to Mars\n       </b>\n       has been the subject of\n       <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">\n        science fiction\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">\n        aerospace engineering\n       </a>\n       , and scientific proposals since the 19th century. The plans comprise proposals to land on\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       , eventually\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars" title="Colonization of Mars">\n        settling on\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Terraforming_of_Mars" title="Terraforming of Mars">\n        terraforming the planet\n       </a>\n       , while utilizing its moons,\n       <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">\n        Phobos\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Deimos_(moon)" title="Deimos (moon)">\n        Deimos\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">\n        exploration of Mars\n       </a>\n       has been a goal of national space programs for decades. Preliminary work for missions that would involve human explorers has been undertaken since the 1950s, with planned missions typically being stated as taking place 10 to 30 years in the future when they are drafted. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_manned_Mars_mission_plans_in_the_20th_century" title="List of manned Mars mission plans in the 20th century">\n        list of manned Mars mission plans in the 20th century\n       </a>\n       shows the various mission proposals that have been put forth by multiple organizations and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_agency" title="Space agency">\n        space agencies\n       </a>\n       in this field of\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">\n        space exploration\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 2010s, numerous Chinese, European and American agencies were developing proposals for human missions to Mars. None have moved past the planning stages.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_in_fiction" title="Mars in fiction">\n        Mars in fiction\n       </a>\n       is a frequent target of exploration and settlement in books, graphic novels, and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_on_Mars" title="List of films set on Mars">\n        films\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1    <a href="#Inspiration_Mars_Foundation_.282013.29">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               3.2.18\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Inspiration Mars Foundation (2013)\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-35">\n             <a Affordable Mission (2014)\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-36">\n             <a class="toctext">\n               NASA\'s Journey to Mars: Pioneering Next Steps in Space Exploration (2015)\n              </span>\n             </a>\n             <ul>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-37">\n               <a href="#Bolden_speech_.282015.29">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 3.2.20.1\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Bolden speech (2015)\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n             </ul>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-38">\n             <a href="#Interplanetary_Transport_System_.282016.29">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               3.2.21\n              </span>\n       <a href="#Mars_Base_Camp_.282016.29">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               3.2.22\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Mars Base Camp (2016)\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-40">\n             <a href="#Deep_Space_Transport_.282017.29">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               3.2.23\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Deep Space Transport (2017)\n              </span>\n             </a>\n  <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Current intentions by nations and space agencies\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">\n         <a href="#Technological_innovations_and_hurdles">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Technological innovations and hurdles\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">\n         <a href="#Precursor_missions">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Precursor missions\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44">\n           <a href="#Manned_flyby">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Manned flyby\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45">\n           <a href="#Missions_to_Deimos_or_Phobos">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Missions to Deimos or Phobos\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-46">\n           <a href="#Mars_sample_return_missions">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mars sample return missions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 orbital missions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_to_Mars">\n        Travel to Mars\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Travel to Mars">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1541" data-file-width="2675" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg/220px-Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg/330px-Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg/440px-Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_Globes_of_Mars.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Three views of planet Mars, the "red planet"\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_close_appr.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="444" data-file-width="759" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mars_close_appr.png/330px-Mars_close_appr.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mars_close_appr.png/495px-Mars_close_appr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mars_close_appr.png/660px-Mars_close_appr.png 2x" width="330"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_close_appr.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Closest approaches of Mars to Earth, 2014-2061. Communication times are slightly shorter when it is closest.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The energy needed for transfer between planetary orbits, or "\n       <a href="/wiki/Delta-v" title="Delta-v">\n        \xe2\x88\x86V\n       </a>\n       ", is lowest at intervals fixed by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synodic_period" title="Synodic period">\n        synodic period\n       </a>\n       . For Earth / Mars trips, this is every 26 months (2 years and 2 months),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       so missions are typically planned to coincide with one of these\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_window" title="Launch window">\n        launch windows\n       </a>\n       . The energy needed in the low-energy windows varies on roughly a 15-year cycle\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the easiest windows needing only half the energy of the peaks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001window_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001window-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 20th century, there was a minimum in the 1969 and 1971 launch windows and another low in 1986 and 1988, then the cycle repeated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several types of mission plans have been proposed, such as the opposition class and conjunction class,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001window_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001window-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crocco_Grand_Tour" title="Crocco Grand Tour">\n        Crocco flyby\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001flyby_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001flyby-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lowest energy transfer to Mars is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Hohmann_transfer_orbit" title="Hohmann transfer orbit">\n        Hohmann transfer orbit\n       </a>\n       ; a mission to Mars using Hohmann transfer involves an approximately 9 month travel time from Earth to Mars, about five hundred days at Mars to wait for the transfer window to Earth, and a Hohmann transfer of about 9 months to return to Earth.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shorter Mars mission plans have round-trip flight times of 400 to 450 days,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vonBraun_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vonBraun-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but requiring a higher energy. A fast Mars mission of 245 days round trip could be possible with on-orbit staging.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2014\n       <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_capture" title="Ballistic capture">\n        ballistic capture\n       </a>\n       was proposed, which may reduce fuel cost and provide more flexible launch windows compared to the Hohmann.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the Crocco grand tour, a crewed spacecraft would get a flyby of Mars and Venus for under a year in space.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some flyby mission architectures can also be extended to include a style of Mars landing with a flyby excursion lander spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired.com_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wired.com-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Proposed by R. Titus in 1966, it involved extending a flyby mission with a short stay lander.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired.com_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wired.com-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Basically, a short stay lander-ascent vehicle would separate from a "parent" Earth-Mars transfer prior to its flyby of Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired.com_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wired.com-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ascent-Decent lander would arrive sooner and either go into orbit around Mars or land, and depending on the design offer perhaps 10\xe2\x80\x9330 days before it needed to launch itself back to the main transfer vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired.com_8-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wired.com-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (see also\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_flyby" title="Mars flyby">\n        Mars flyby\n       </a>\n       )\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Challenges">\n        Challenges\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Challenges">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Logistical">\n        Logistical\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Logistical">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The estimated cost of sending humans to Mars is roughly 500 billion U.S. dollars, though the actual costs are likely to be more.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The largest limiting factor for sending humans to Mars is funding. In the late 1950s, rivalry between the Soviet Union and the United States stimulated a national priority to send humans to the Moon. Under the current global geopolitical climate, however, government funding of these programs has decreased. Recent participation of private companies in space travel and participation by new nations such as India\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       may present new opportunities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Critics argue the immediate benefits of establishing a human presence on Mars are more esoteric than practical. Yet proponents of human space exploration contend that while the short term benefits will be academic, the symbolism of establishing a presence in space may garner public interest to join the cause and spark global cooperation. Furthermore, experts maintain that a long-term investment will be necessary for humanity\xe2\x80\x99s survival.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical">\n        Physical\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Physical">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="1024" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg/240px-Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg/360px-Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg/480px-Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg 2x" width="240"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nasa_mars_artificial_gravity_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         In the artistic vision, the spacecraft provides\n         <a href="/wiki/Artificial_gravity" title="Artificial gravity">\n          artificial gravity\n         </a>\n         by spinning. (see also\n         <a href="/wiki/Centrifugal_force" title="Centrifugal force">\n          Centrifugal force\n         </a>\n         )\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="900" height="373" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/330px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/495px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/660px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 2x" width="330"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Comparison of radiation doses - includes the amount detected on the trip from Earth to Mars by the\n         <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n          RAD\n         </a>\n         inside the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n          MSL\n         </a>\n         (2011 - 2013).\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_11-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-11">\n           [11]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531b_12-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531b-12">\n           [12]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130530_13-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130530-13">\n           [13]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The vertical axis is in\n         <a href="/wiki/Logarithmic_scale" title="Logarithmic scale">\n          logarithmic scale\n         </a>\n         , so the dose over a Mars year is about 15 times the DOE limit, not less than twice, as a quick glance might suggest. The actual dose would depend on a number of factors such as design of the spacecraft and natural events such as\n         <a href="/wiki/Solar_flare" title="Solar flare">\n          Solar flares\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There are several key physical challenges for human missions to Mars:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150921_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150921-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays" title="Health threat from cosmic rays">\n         Health threats\n        </a>\n        from exposure to high-energy cosmic rays and other\n        <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">\n         ionizing radiation\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n         <a href="#cite_note-15">\n          [15]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n         <a href="#cite_note-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WIRED-20140212_17-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WIRED-20140212-17">\n          [17]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In May 2013, NASA scientists reported that a possible mission to Mars may involve a great\n        <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n         radiation risk\n        </a>\n        based on the amount of\n        <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n         energetic particle radiation\n        </a>\n        detected by the\n        <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n         RAD\n        </a>\n        on the\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n         Mars Science Laboratory\n        </a>\n        while traveling from the\n        <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n         Earth\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n         Mars\n        </a>\n        in 2011-2012. The calculated radiation dose was 0.66\n        <a href="/wiki/Sievert" title="Sievert">\n         sieverts\n        </a>\n        round-trip. The agency\'s career radiation limit for astronauts is 1 sievert.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_11-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-11">\n          [11]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531b_12-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531b-12">\n          [12]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130530_13-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130530-13">\n          [13]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SN-20130629_18-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-SN-20130629-18">\n          [18]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In September 2017, NASA reported\n        <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n         radiation levels\n        </a>\n        on the surface of the planet\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n         Mars\n        </a>\n        were temporarily\n        <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(radiation)" title="Orders of magnitude (radiation)">\n         doubled\n        </a>\n        , and were associated with an\n        <a href="/wiki/Aurora" title="Aurora">\n         aurora\n        </a>\n        25-times brighter than any observed earlier, due to a massive, and unexpected,\n        <a href="/wiki/Coronal_mass_ejection" title="Coronal mass ejection">\n         solar storm\n        </a>\n        in the middle of the month.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHYS-20170930_19-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-PHYS-20170930-19">\n          [19]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Weightlessness#Human_health_effects" title="Weightlessness">\n         Negative effects\n        </a>\n        of a\n        <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_spaceflight_on_the_human_body" title="Effect of spaceflight on the human body">\n         prolonged weightlessness environment on human health\n        </a>\n        , including\n        <a href="/wiki/Visual_impairment_due_to_intracranial_pressure" title="Visual impairment due to intracranial pressure">\n         eyesight visual impairment\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mader-2011_20-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Mader-2011-20">\n          [20]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puiu-20111109_21-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Puiu-20111109-21">\n          [21]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-20120109_22-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-CNN-20120109-22">\n          [22]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        (Depends on mission and spacecraft design).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Psychological effects of isolation from Earth and, by extension, the lack of community due to impossibility of real-time connections with Earth. (Compare\n        <a href="/wiki/Hermit" title="Hermit">\n         Hermit\n        </a>\n        ).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Social effects of several humans living under cramped conditions for more than one Earth year, possibly two or three years, on the mission to Mars, and a comparable length of time on the return to Earth. (Depends on spacecraft and mission design).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Inaccessibility of terrestrial medical facilities.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Potential failure of propulsion or life-support equipment.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Some of these issues were estimated statistically in the HUMEX study.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ehlmann and others have reviewed political and economic concerns, as well as technological and biological feasibility aspects.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While fuel for roundtrip travel could be a challenge, methane and oxygen can be produced using Martian H\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       O (preferably as water ice instead of liquid water) and atmospheric CO\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       with mature technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planetary_protection">\n        Planetary protection\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Planetary protection">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_protection" title="Planetary protection">\n        Planetary protection\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Robotic spacecraft to Mars are required to be sterilized, to have at most 300,000 spores on the exterior of the craft\xe2\x80\x94and more thoroughly sterilized if they contact "special regions" containing water,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-groundwatercontamination_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-groundwatercontamination-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COSPAR_PLANETARY_PROTECTION_POLICY_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-COSPAR_PLANETARY_PROTECTION_POLICY-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as otherwise there is a risk of contaminating not only the life-detection experiments but possibly the planet itself.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is impossible to sterilize human missions to this level, as humans are host to typically a hundred trillion microorganisms of thousands of species of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_microbiome" title="Human microbiome">\n        human microbiome\n       </a>\n       , and these cannot be removed while preserving the life of the human. Containment seems the only option, but it is a major challenge in the event of a hard landing (i.e. crash).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biospherescollide_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-biospherescollide-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There have been several planetary workshops on this issue, but with no final guidelines for a way forward yet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Human explorers would also be vulnerable to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Back_contamination" title="Back contamination">\n        back contamination\n       </a>\n       to Earth if they become carriers of microorganisms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_proposals">\n        Mission proposals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mission proposals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_manned_Mars_mission_plans" title="List of manned Mars mission plans">\n        List of manned Mars mission plans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">\n        20th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S86_25375patraw.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4475" data-file-width="3014" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/S86_25375patraw.jpg/170px-S86_25375patraw.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/S86_25375patraw.jpg/255px-S86_25375patraw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/S86_25375patraw.jpg/340px-S86_25375patraw.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S86_25375patraw.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Fuel is mined from Phobos with the help of a nuclear reactor.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n          <a href="#cite_note-32">\n           [32]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Over the last century, a number of mission concepts for such an expedition have been proposed. David Portree\'s history volume\n       <i>\n        Humans to Mars: Fifty Years of Mission Planning, 1950\xe2\x80\x932000\n       </i>\n       discusses many of these.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Wernher_von_Braun_proposal_(1947_through_1950s)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wernher_von_Braun_proposal_.281947_through_1950s.29">\n        Wernher von Braun proposal (1947 through 1950s)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Wernher von Braun proposal (1947 through 1950s)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">\n        Wernher von Braun\n       </a>\n       was the first person to make a detailed technical study of a Mars mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portree2001_1-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portree2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-platoff_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-platoff-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Details were published in his book\n       <i>\n        Das Marsprojekt\n       </i>\n       (1952, published in English as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Mars_Project" title="The Mars Project">\n         The Mars Project\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in 1962\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) and several subsequent works,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and featured in\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collier%27s_magazine" title="Collier\'s magazine">\n         Collier\'s magazine\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in a series of articles beginning March 1952. A variant of the Von Braun mission concept was popularized in English by\n       <a href="/wiki/Willy_Ley" title="Willy Ley">\n        Willy Ley\n       </a>\n       in the book\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Conquest_of_Space" title="The Conquest of Space">\n         The Conquest of Space\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (1949), featuring illustrations by\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesley_Bonestell" title="Chesley Bonestell">\n        Chesley Bonestell\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title=\'"It\'>\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Von Braun\'s Mars project envisioned nearly a thousand three-stage vehicles launching from Earth to ferry parts for the Mars mission to be constructed at a space station in Earth orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-platoff_33-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-platoff-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The mission itself featured a fleet of ten spacecraft with a combined crew of 70 heading to Mars, bringing three winged surface excursion ships that would land horizontally on the surface of Mars. (Winged landing was considered possible because at the time of his proposal, the Martian atmosphere was believed to be much denser than was later found to be the case.)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1956 revised vision of the Mars Project plan, published in the book\n       <i>\n        The Exploration of Mars\n       </i>\n       by Wernher Von Braun and Willy Ley, the size of the mission was trimmed, requiring only 400 launches to put together two ships, still carrying a winged landing vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later versions of the mission proposal, featured in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">\n        Disney\n       </a>\n       "Man In Space" film series,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       showed\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">\n        nuclear-powered\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_propulsion" title="Ion propulsion">\n        ion-propulsion\n       </a>\n       vehicles for the interplanetary cruise.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="U.S._proposals_(1950s,_1960s,_and_1970s)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._proposals_.281950s.2C_1960s.2C_and_1970s.29">\n        U.S. proposals (1950s, 1960s, and 1970s)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: U.S. proposals (1950s, 1960s, and 1970s)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="975" data-file-width="1400" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg/220px-Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg/330px-Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg/440px-Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Excursion_Module.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist\'s conception of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mars_Excursion_Module" title="Mars Excursion Module">\n          Mars Excursion Module\n         </a>\n         (MEM) proposed in a NASA study in 1963.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1962, Aeronutronic Ford,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dixon_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dixon-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       General Dynamics and the Lockheed Missiles and Space Company made studies of Mars mission designs as part of NASA Marshall Spaceflight Center "\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Project_EMPIRE&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Project EMPIRE (page does not exist)">\n        Project EMPIRE\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-platoff_33-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-platoff-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These studies indicated that a Mars mission (possibly including a Venus fly-by) could be done with a launch of eight Saturn V boosters and assembly in low Earth orbit, or possibly with a single launch of a hypothetical "post Saturn" heavy-lift vehicle. Although the EMPIRE missions were only studies, and never proposed as funded projects, these were the first detailed analyses of what it would take to accomplish a human voyage to Mars using data from actual NASA spaceflight, and laid much of the basis for future studies, including significant mission studies by TRW, North American, Philco, Lockheed, Douglas, and General Dynamics, along with several in-house NASA studies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-platoff_33-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-platoff-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the success of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_Program" title="Apollo Program">\n        Apollo Program\n       </a>\n       , von Braun advocated a manned mission to Mars as a focus for NASA\'s manned space program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Von Braun\'s proposal used\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       boosters to launch nuclear-powered (\n       <a href="/wiki/NERVA" title="NERVA">\n        NERVA\n       </a>\n       ) upper stages that would power two six-crew spacecraft on a dual mission in the early 1980s. The proposal was considered by (then president)\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">\n        Richard Nixon\n       </a>\n       but passed over in favor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1975, von Braun discussed the mission architecture that emerged from these Apollo-era studies in a recorded lecture and while doing so suggested that multiple\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Shuttle\n       </a>\n       launches could instead be configured to lift the two Nuclear Thermal Rocket engine equipped spacecrafts in smaller parts, for assembly in-orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Soviet_mission_proposals_(1956_through_1969)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_mission_proposals_.281956_through_1969.29">\n        Soviet mission proposals (1956 through 1969)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Soviet mission proposals (1956 through 1969)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Martian_Piloted_Complex" title="Martian Piloted Complex">\n        Martian Piloted Complex\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/TMK" title="TMK">\n        TMK\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Martian_Piloted_Complex" title="Martian Piloted Complex">\n        Martian Piloted Complex\n       </a>\n       or "\'MPK\'" was a proposal by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Tikhonravov" title="Mikhail Tikhonravov">\n        Mikhail Tikhonravov\n       </a>\n       of the Soviet Union for a manned Mars expedition, using the (then proposed) N-1 rocket, in studies from 1956 to 1962. The Soviets sent many probes to Mars with some noted success stories including Mars atmospheric entry, but the ratio was low and their space program struggled through disasters like the lost\n       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">\n        Salyut 1\n       </a>\n       crew and explosions of their N-1 rocket (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_3" title="Mars 3">\n        Mars 3\n       </a>\n       )\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/TMK" title="TMK">\n        Heavy Interplanetary Spacecraft\n       </a>\n       (known by the Russian acronym\n       <b>\n        TMK\n       </b>\n       ) was the designation of a Soviet Union space exploration proposal in the 1960s to send a manned flight to Mars and Venus (TMK-MAVR design) without landing. The TMK spacecraft was due to launch in 1971 and make a three-year-long flight including a Mars fly-by at which time probes would have been dropped. The project was never completed because the required\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N1_rocket" title="N1 rocket">\n        N1 rocket\n       </a>\n       never flew successfully. The\n       <i>\n        Mars Expeditionary Complex\n       </i>\n       , or "\'MEK"\' (1969) was another Soviet proposal for a Mars expedition that would take a crew from three to six to Mars and back with a total mission duration of 630 days.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Case_for_Mars_(1981\xe2\x80\x931996)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Case_for_Mars_.281981.E2.80.931996.29">\n        Case for Mars (1981\xe2\x80\x931996)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Case for Mars (1981\xe2\x80\x931996)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Following the\n       <a href="/wiki/Viking_program" title="Viking program">\n        Viking\n       </a>\n       missions to Mars, between 1981 and 1996 a series of conferences named The Case for Mars were held at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Colorado_at_Boulder" title="University of Colorado at Boulder">\n        University of Colorado at Boulder\n       </a>\n       . These conferences advocated human exploration of Mars, presented concepts and technologies, and held a series of workshops to develop a baseline concept for the mission. The baseline concept was notable in that it proposed use of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-situ_resource_utilization" title="In-situ resource utilization">\n        in-situ resource utilization\n       </a>\n       to manufacture rocket propellant for the return trip using the resources of Mars. The mission study was published in a series of proceedings volumes\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       published by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Astronautical_Society" title="American Astronautical Society">\n        American Astronautical Society\n       </a>\n       . Later conferences in the series presented a number of alternative concepts, including the "Mars Direct" concept of\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zubrin" title="Robert Zubrin">\n        Robert Zubrin\n       </a>\n       and David Baker; the "Footsteps to Mars" proposal of\n       <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_A._Landis" title="Geoffrey A. Landis">\n        Geoffrey A. Landis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footstepstomars_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-footstepstomars-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which proposed intermediate steps before the landing on Mars, including human missions to Phobos; and the "Great Exploration" proposal from\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Livermore_National_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory">\n        Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory\n       </a>\n       , among others.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Space_Exploration_Initiative_(1989)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Space_Exploration_Initiative_.281989.29">\n        NASA Space Exploration Initiative (1989)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: NASA Space Exploration Initiative (1989)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Exploration_Initiative" title="Space Exploration Initiative">\n        Space Exploration Initiative\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_mission.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1393" data-file-width="2032" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mars_mission.jpg/220px-Mars_mission.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mars_mission.jpg/330px-Mars_mission.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mars_mission.jpg/440px-Mars_mission.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_mission.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist\'s conception of a human mission on the surface of Mars\n         <br/>\n         1989 painting by Les Bossinas of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lewis_Research_Center" title="Lewis Research Center">\n          Lewis Research Center\n         </a>\n         for NASA\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In response to a presidential initiative, NASA made a study of a project for human lunar- and Mars exploration as a proposed follow-on to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       project. This resulted in a report, called the\n       <i>\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=90-day_study&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="90-day study (page does not exist)">\n         90-day study\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in which the agency proposed a long-term plan consisting of completing the Space Station as "a critical next step in all our space endeavors," returning to the moon and establishing a permanent base, and then sending astronauts to Mars. This report was widely criticized as too elaborate and expensive, and all funding for human exploration beyond Earth orbit was canceled by Congress.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Mars_Direct_(early_1990s)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_Direct_.28early_1990s.29">\n        Mars Direct (early 1990s)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mars Direct (early 1990s)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Direct" title="Mars Direct">\n        Mars Direct\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Because of the distance between Mars and Earth, the Mars mission would be much more risky and more expensive than past manned flights to the Moon, supplies and fuel would have to be prepared for a 2-3 year round trip and the spacecraft would have to be designed with at least partial shielding from intense solar radiation. A 1990 paper by\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zubrin" title="Robert Zubrin">\n        Robert Zubrin\n       </a>\n       and David A. Baker, then of\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Marietta" title="Martin Marietta">\n        Martin Marietta\n       </a>\n       , proposed reducing the mission mass (and hence the cost) with a mission design using\n       <a href="/wiki/In_situ_resource_utilization#Mars" title="In situ resource utilization">\n        in situ resource utilization\n       </a>\n       to manufacture propellant from the Martian Atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This proposal drew on a number of concepts developed by the former "\n       <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080621011517/http://spot.colorado.edu/~marscase/Home.html" rel="nofollow">\n        Case for Mars\n       </a>\n       " conference series. Over the next decade, this proposal was developed by Zubrin into a mission concept,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Direct" title="Mars Direct">\n        Mars Direct\n       </a>\n       , which he developed in a book,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Case_for_Mars" title="The Case for Mars">\n         The Case for Mars\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (1996). The mission is advocated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Society" title="Mars Society">\n        Mars Society\n       </a>\n       , which Zubrin founded in 1998, as a practical and affordable plan for a manned Mars mission.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="International_Space_University_(1991)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="International_Space_University_.281991.29">\n        International Space University (1991)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International Space University (1991)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 1991 in Toulouse, France, the International Space University studied an international human Mars mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mendell_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mendell-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They proposed a crew of 8 traveling to Mars in a nuclear-powered vessel with artificial gravity provided by rotation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mendell_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mendell-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the surface, 40 tonne habitats pressurized to 10\xc2\xa0psi (69\xc2\xa0kPa) were powered by a 40\xc2\xa0kW photovoltaic array.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mendell_49-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mendell-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Design_reference_missions_(1990s)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Design_reference_missions_.281990s.29">\n        NASA Design reference missions (1990s)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: NASA Design reference missions (1990s)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Design_Reference_Mission" title="Mars Design Reference Mission">\n        Mars Design Reference Mission\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3655" data-file-width="4617" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg/220px-Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg/330px-Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg/440px-Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_design_reference_mission_3.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NASA Mars habitat concept for DRA 1.0, derived from the Mars Direct Architecture. (1995)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the 1990s NASA developed several conceptual level human Mars exploration architectures. One of these was NASA\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Design_reference_mission_3.0" title="Design reference mission 3.0">\n        Design reference mission 3.0\n       </a>\n       (DRM 3.0). It was a study performed by the NASA Mars Exploration Team at the NASA\'s Johnson Space Center (JSC) in the 1990s. Personnel representing several NASA field centers formulated a "Reference Mission" addressing human exploration of Mars. The plan describes a human mission to Mars with concepts of operations and technologies to be used as a first cut at an architecture. The architecture for the Mars Reference Mission builds on previous work, principally on the work of the Synthesis Group (1991) and Zubrin\'s (1991) concepts for the use of propellants derived from the Martian atmosphere. The primary purpose of the Reference Mission was to stimulate further thought and development of alternative approaches, which can improve effectiveness, reduce risks, and reduce cost. Improvements can be made at several levels; for example, in the architectural, mission, and system levels.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Selected other US/NASA plans (1988\xe2\x80\x932009):\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trs-new.jpl.nasa.gov_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-trs-new.jpl.nasa.gov-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ol>\n       <li>\n        1988 "Mars Expedition"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1989 "Mars Evolution"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1990 "90-Day Study"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1991 "Synthesis Group"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1995 "DRM 1"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1997 "DRM 3"\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n         <a href="#cite_note-51">\n          [51]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1998 "DRM 4"\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1999 "Dual Landers"\n       </li>\n      </ol>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">\n        21st century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 21st century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manned_mission_to_Mars_(artist%27s_concept).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3555" height="155" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Manned_mission_to_Mars_%28artist%27s_concept%29.jpg/550px-Manned_mission_to_Mars_%28artist%27s_concept%29.jpg 2x" width="275"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manned_mission_to_Mars_(artist%27s_concept).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Crew members setting up weather monitoring equipment on the surface of Mars (artist\'s concept)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Design_reference_missions_(2000+)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Design_reference_missions_.282000.2B.29">\n        NASA Design reference missions (2000+)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: NASA Design reference missions (2000+)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Design_Reference_Mission" title="Mars Design Reference Mission">\n        Mars Design Reference Missions\n       </a>\n       consisted of a series of conceptual design studies for human Mars missions, continued in the 21st century Selected other US/NASA plans (1988\xe2\x80\x932009):\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trs-new.jpl.nasa.gov_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-trs-new.jpl.nasa.gov-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div>\n       <ol start="11">\n        <li>\n         2000 SERT (SSP)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         2001 DPT/NEXT\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         2002 NEP Art. Gravity\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         2009 DRA 5\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n          <a href="#cite_note-52">\n           [52]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </li>\n       </ol>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="MARPOST_(2000\xe2\x80\x932005)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="MARPOST_.282000.E2.80.932005.29">\n        MARPOST (2000\xe2\x80\x932005)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: MARPOST (2000\xe2\x80\x932005)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Piloted_Orbital_Station" title="Mars Piloted Orbital Station">\n        Mars Piloted Orbital Station\n       </a>\n       (or MARPOST) is a Russian proposed manned orbital mission to Mars, using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">\n        nuclear reactor\n       </a>\n       to run an electric rocket engine. Proposed in October 2000 by Yuri Karash from the Russian Academy of Cosmonautics as the next step for Russia in space along with the Russian participation in the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       , a 30-volume draft project for MARPOST was confirmed as of 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Design for the ship was proposed to be ready in 2012, and the ship itself in 2021.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="ESA_Aurora_programme_(2001+)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ESA_Aurora_programme_.282001.2B.29">\n        ESA Aurora programme (2001+)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: ESA Aurora programme (2001+)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Aurora_programme" title="Aurora programme">\n        Aurora programme\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4275" data-file-width="3989" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg/220px-Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg/330px-Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg/440px-Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars-human-exploration-art-astronauts-vehicle-dust-full.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artwork featuring astronauts enduring a Mars dust storm near a rover\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       had a long-term vision of sending a human mission to Mars in 2033.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Laid out in 2001, the project\'s proposed timeline would begin with robotic exploration, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_concept" title="Proof of concept">\n        proof of concept\n       </a>\n       simulation of sustaining humans on Mars, and eventually a manned mission; however, objections from the participating nations of ESA and other delays have put the timeline into question. Nevertheless, a spawn of this programme,\n       <a href="/wiki/ExoMars" title="ExoMars">\n        ExoMars\n       </a>\n       , delivered an orbiter to Mars in 2016\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="ESA/Russia_plan_(2002)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ESA.2FRussia_plan_.282002.29">\n        ESA/Russia plan (2002)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: ESA/Russia plan (2002)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Another proposal for a joint ESA mission with Russia is based on two spacecraft being sent to Mars, one carrying a six-person crew and the other the expedition\'s supplies. The mission would take about 440 days to complete with three astronauts visiting the surface of the planet for a period of two months. The entire project would cost $20 billion and Russia would contribute 30% of these funds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="USA_Vision_for_Space_Exploration_(2004)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="USA_Vision_for_Space_Exploration_.282004.29">\n        USA Vision for Space Exploration (2004)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: USA Vision for Space Exploration (2004)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n        Vision for Space Exploration\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vsfe_ship.jpg">\n         <img alt="Vsfe ship.jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vsfe_ship.jpg/220px-Vsfe_ship.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vsfe_ship.jpg/330px-Vsfe_ship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/Vsfe_ship.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vsfe_ship.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Constellation" title="Project Constellation">\n        Project Constellation\n       </a>\n       included an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Mars_Mission" title="Orion Mars Mission">\n        Orion Mars Mission\n       </a>\n       . (Then United States President)\n       <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n        George W. Bush\n       </a>\n       announced an initiative of manned space exploration on January 14, 2004, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n        Vision for Space Exploration\n       </a>\n       . It included developing preliminary plans for a lunar outpost by 2012\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and establishing an outpost by 2020. Precursor missions that would help develop the needed technology during the 2010-2020 decade were tentatively outlined by Adringa and others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On September 24, 2007, Michael Griffin, then NASA Administrator, hinted that NASA may be able to launch a human mission to Mars by 2037.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The needed funds were to be generated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n        diverting $11 billion\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       from space science missions to the vision for human exploration.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA has also discussed plans to launch Mars missions from the Moon to reduce traveling costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Mars_Society_Germany_-_European_Mars_Mission_(EMM)_(2005)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_Society_Germany_-_European_Mars_Mission_.28EMM.29_.282005.29">\n        Mars Society Germany - European Mars Mission (EMM) (2005)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mars Society Germany - European Mars Mission (EMM) (2005)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The Mars Society Germany proposed a manned Mars mission using several launches of an improved heavy-lift version of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       . Roughly 5 launches would be required to send a crew of 5 on a 1200 days mission, with a payload of 120,000\xc2\xa0kg (260,000\xc2\xa0lb). Total project was estimated to cost 10 to 15 billion\n       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\n        Euros\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronautix.com_62-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astronautix.com-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="China_National_Space_Administration_(CNSA)_(2006)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="China_National_Space_Administration_.28CNSA.29_.282006.29">\n        China National Space Administration (CNSA) (2006)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: China National Space Administration (CNSA) (2006)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_space_program#Mission_to_Mars_and_beyond" title="Chinese space program">\n        Chinese space program \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Mission to Mars and beyond\n       </a>\n      </div>\n
