<p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun_Laiyan" title="Sun Laiyan">\n        Sun Laiyan\n       </a>\n       , administrator of the\n       <a href="/wiki/China_National_Space_Administration" title="China National Space Administration">\n        China National Space Administration\n       </a>\n       , said on July 20, 2006 that China would start deep space exploration focusing on\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       over the next five years, during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleventh_Five-Year_Plan_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" title="Eleventh Five-Year Plan (People\'s Republic of China)">\n        Eleventh Five-Year Plan\n       </a>\n       (2006\xe2\x80\x932010) Program period.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first uncrewed Mars exploration program could take place between 2014\xe2\x80\x932033, followed by a crewed phase in 2040-2060 in which crew members would land on Mars and return home.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_500" title="Mars 500">\n        Mars 500\n       </a>\n       study of 2011 prepared for this manned mission.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="The_One-Way_Trip_Option_(2006);_Mars_to_Stay_(2006)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_One-Way_Trip_Option_.282006.29.3B_Mars_to_Stay_.282006.29">\n        The One-Way Trip Option (2006); Mars to Stay (2006)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The One-Way Trip Option (2006); Mars to Stay (2006)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_to_Stay" title="Mars to Stay">\n        Mars to Stay\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The idea of a one-way trip to Mars has been proposed several times. Space activist Bruce Mackenzie, for example, proposed a one-way trip to Mars in a presentation "One Way to Mars - a Permanent Settlement on the First Mission" at the 1998\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Development_Conference" title="International Space Development Conference">\n        International Space Development Conference\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       arguing that since the mission could be done with less difficulty and expense if the astronauts were not required to return to Earth, the first mission to Mars should be a settlement, not a visit. In 2006, former NASA engineer James C. McLane III proposed a scheme to initially colonize Mars via a one-way trip by only one human. Papers discussing this concept appeared in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Space_Review" title="The Space Review">\n         The Space Review\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Magazine" title="Harper\'s Magazine">\n         Harper\'s Magazine\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        SEARCH Magazine\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n         The New York Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krauss_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Krauss-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mars to Stay proposes that astronauts sent to Mars for the first time should stay there indefinitely, both to reduce mission cost and to ensure permanent settlement of Mars. Among many notable Mars to Stay advocates, former\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo" title="Apollo">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">\n        Buzz Aldrin\n       </a>\n       is a particularly outspoken promoter who has suggested in numerous forums "Forget the Moon, Let\'s Head to Mars!"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In June 2013, Aldrin wrote an opinion, published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n         The New York Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , supporting a manned mission to Mars and which viewed the moon "not as a destination but more a point of departure, one that places humankind on a trajectory to homestead Mars and become a two-planet species."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130613_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130613-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In August 2015, Aldrin, in association with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Institute_of_Technology" title="Florida Institute of Technology">\n        Florida Institute of Technology\n       </a>\n       , presented a "master plan" for NASA consideration proposing astronauts with a "tour of duty of ten years" colonize Mars before the year 2040.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150827_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20150827-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Design_Reference_Mission_5.0_(2007)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Design_Reference_Mission_5.0_.282007.29">\n        NASA Design Reference Mission 5.0 (2007)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: NASA Design Reference Mission 5.0 (2007)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       NASA released initial details of the latest version conceptual level human Mars exploration architecture in\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.lpi.usra.edu/meetings/leag2007/presentations/20071001.drake.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n        this\n       </a>\n       presentation. The study further developed concepts developed in previous NASA DRM and updated it to more current launchers and technology.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Design_Reference_Mission_Architecture_5.0_(2009)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Design_Reference_Mission_Architecture_5.0_.282009.29">\n        NASA Design Reference Mission Architecture 5.0 (2009)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: NASA Design Reference Mission Architecture 5.0 (2009)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="642" data-file-width="1438" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg/220px-Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg/330px-Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg/440px-Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars-manned-mission-NASA-V5.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Concept for NASA\'s Design Reference Mission Architecture 5.0 (2009)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       NASA released an updated version of NASA DRM 5.0 in early 2009, featuring use of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_V" title="Ares V">\n        Ares V\n       </a>\n       launcher,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion CEV\n       </a>\n       , and updated mission planning. In\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.lpi.usra.edu/meetings/leag2007/presentations/20071001.drake.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n        this\n       </a>\n       document.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA_Austere_Human_Missions_to_Mars_(2009)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Austere_Human_Missions_to_Mars_.282009.29">\n        NASA\n        <a href="/wiki/Austere_Human_Missions_to_Mars" title="Austere Human Missions to Mars">\n         Austere Human Missions to Mars\n        </a>\n        (2009)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: NASA Austere Human Missions to Mars (2009)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Extrapolated from the DRMA 5.0, plans for a manned Mars expedition with chemical propulsion.\n       <a class="external text" href="http://trs-new.jpl.nasa.gov/dspace/bitstream/2014/41431/1/09-3642.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n        Austere Human Missions to Mars\n       </a>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="USA\'s_Mars_orbit_by_the_mid-2030s_(2010)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="USA.27s_Mars_orbit_by_the_mid-2030s_.282010.29">\n        USA\'s Mars orbit by the mid-2030s (2010)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: USA\'s Mars orbit by the mid-2030s (2010)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_space_policy_speech_at_Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Barack Obama space policy speech at Kennedy Space Center">\n        major space policy speech\n       </a>\n       at Kennedy Space Center on April 15, 2010, former U.S. President\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       predicted a manned Mars mission to orbit the planet by the mid-2030s, followed by a landing:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        By the mid-2030s, I believe we can send humans to orbit Mars and return them safely to Earth. And a landing on Mars will follow. And I expect to be around to see it.\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       The United States Congress has mostly approved a new direction for NASA that includes canceling Bush\'s planned return to the Moon by 2020 and instead proposes asteroid exploration in 2025 (\n       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_Redirect_Mission" title="Asteroid Redirect Mission">\n        Asteroid Redirect Mission\n       </a>\n       ) and orbiting Mars in the 2030s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Martian_Frontier_(2007-_2011)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Martian_Frontier_.282007-_2011.29">\n        Martian Frontier (2007- 2011)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Martian Frontier (2007- 2011)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Mars 500, the longest high fidelity spaceflight simulation, ran from 2007 to 2011 in Russia and was an experiment to assess the feasibility of manned missions to mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Russian_mission_proposals_(2011)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_mission_proposals_.282011.29">\n        Russian mission proposals (2011)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Russian mission proposals (2011)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       A number of Mars mission concepts and proposals have been put forth by\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       scientists. Stated dates were for a launch sometime between 2016 and 2020. The Mars probe would carry a crew of four to five cosmonauts, who would spend close to two years in space.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In late 2011, Russian and European space agencies successfully completed the ground-based\n       <a href="/wiki/MARS-500" title="MARS-500">\n        MARS-500\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The biomedical experiment simulating manned flight to Mars was completed in Russia in July 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="2-4-2_concept_(2011\xe2\x80\x932012)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2-4-2_concept_.282011.E2.80.932012.29">\n        2-4-2 concept (2011\xe2\x80\x932012)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 2-4-2 concept (2011\xe2\x80\x932012)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 2011, Jean-Marc Salotti published a new proposal for a manned Mars mission, with a release in 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 2-4-2 concept is based on a reduction of the crew size to only 2 astronauts and the duplication of the entire mission. There are 2 astronauts in each space vehicle, there are 4 on the surface of Mars and there are 2 once again in each return vehicle. In addition, at every step of the mission, there are 2 astronauts ready to help the 2 others (2 for 2). This architecture simplifies the entry, descent and landing procedures, which are known to be very risky, thanks to a significant reduction of the size of the landing vehicles. It also avoids the assembly of huge vehicles in LEO. The author claims that his proposal is much cheaper than the NASA reference mission without compromising the risks and can be undertaken before 2030.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Conceptual_Space_Vehicle_Architecture_for_Human_Exploration_of_Mars_(2012)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conceptual_Space_Vehicle_Architecture_for_Human_Exploration_of_Mars_.282012.29">\n        Conceptual Space Vehicle Architecture for Human Exploration of Mars (2012)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Conceptual Space Vehicle Architecture for Human Exploration of Mars (2012)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 2012,\n       <i>\n        Conceptual Space Vehicle Architecture for Human Exploration of Mars, with Artificial Gravity and Mini-Magnetosphere Crew Radiation Shield\n       </i>\n       was released, laying out a possible design for a human Mars mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Components of the architecture include various spacecraft for the Earth-to-Mars journey, landing, and surface stay as well as return.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some features include a several unmanned cargo landers assembled into a base on the surface of Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The crew would land at this base in the "Mars Personnel Lander", which could also take them back into Mars orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The design for the manned interplanetary spacecraft included artificial-gravity and an artificial magnetic field.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, the architecture was modular and to allow for incremental R&amp;D.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_80-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Mars_One_(2012)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_One_.282012.29">\n        Mars One (2012)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mars One (2012)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_One" title="Mars One">\n        Mars One\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2012, a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Netherlands" title="The Netherlands">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       entrepreneur group began raising funds for a human Mars base to be established in 2023.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adario_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-adario-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One difference from many other humans-to-Mars projects is that the mission is intended to be primarily a settlement mission with no return trip to Earth planned. Astronaut applications were invited from the public all over the world.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The initial plan included that a telecom orbiter and ISRU demonstration lander would be sent in 2018, followed by a rover in 2020, and the base components in 2024.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adario_81-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-adario-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The base would be powered by 3,000 square meters of solar panels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m1_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-m1-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Mars One suggested it could use a\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Heavy\n       </a>\n       rocket to launch flight hardware,.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adario_81-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-adario-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first crew of four astronauts were to land on Mars in 2025. Then, every two years, a new crew of four astronauts would arrive. Plans included selecting and training candidates, and that the entire mission is to be filmed and broadcast back to Earth as a media event. Revenues from broadcasting would help fund the program on top of private investments and monetizing IP rights. In April 2015, Lansdorp admitted that their 12-year plan for landing humans on Mars by 2027 is mostly fiction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Inspiration_Mars_Foundation_(2013)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Inspiration_Mars_Foundation_.282013.29">\n        Inspiration Mars Foundation (2013)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Inspiration Mars Foundation (2013)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Inspiration_Mars_Foundation" title="Inspiration Mars Foundation">\n        Inspiration Mars Foundation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2013, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Inspiration_Mars_Foundation" title="Inspiration Mars Foundation">\n        Inspiration Mars Foundation\n       </a>\n       founded by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Tito" title="Dennis Tito">\n        Dennis Tito\n       </a>\n       revealed plans of a manned mission to fly by Mars in 2018 with support from NASA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Boeing_Affordable_Mission_(2014)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boeing_Affordable_Mission_.282014.29">\n        Boeing Affordable Mission (2014)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Boeing Affordable Mission (2014)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On December 2, 2014, NASA\'s Advanced Human Exploration Systems and Operations Mission Director Jason Crusan and Deputy Associate Administrator for Programs James Reuthner announced tentative support for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       "Affordable Mars Mission Design"\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2016)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       including radiation shielding, centrifugal artificial gravity, in-transit consumable resupply, and a lander which can return.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reuthner suggested that if adequate funding was forthcoming, the proposed mission would be expected in the early 2030s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="NASA\'s_Journey_to_Mars:_Pioneering_Next_Steps_in_Space_Exploration_(2015)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA.27s_Journey_to_Mars:_Pioneering_Next_Steps_in_Space_Exploration_.282015.29">\n        NASA\'s Journey to Mars: Pioneering Next Steps in Space Exploration (2015)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: NASA\'s Journey to Mars: Pioneering Next Steps in Space Exploration (2015)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg/220px-14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg/330px-14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg/440px-14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:14-2290-SpaceLaunchSystem-AfterLaunch-20140827.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist\'s rendering of a Block 1 SLS\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On October 8, 2015, NASA published its official plan for human exploration and colonization of Mars. The plan operates through three distinct phases leading up to fully sustained colonization.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first stage, already underway, is the "Earth Reliant" phase. This phase continues utilizing the International Space Station until 2024; validating deep space technologies and studying the effects of long duration space missions on the human body. The second stage, "Proving Ground," moves away from Earth reliance and ventures into cislunar space for most of its tasks. This is when NASA plans to capture an asteroid (planned for 2020), test deep space habitation facilities, and validate capabilities required for human exploration of Mars. Finally, phase three is the transition to independence from Earth resources. The "Earth Independent" phase includes long term missions on the lunar surface which leverage surface habitats that only require routine maintenance, and the harvesting of Martian resources for fuel, water, and building materials. NASA is still aiming for human missions to Mars in the 2030s, though Earth independence could take decades longer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span id="Bolden_speech_(2015)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bolden_speech_.282015.29">\n        Bolden speech (2015)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Bolden speech (2015)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <p>\n       In November 2015, the administrator of NASA reaffirmed the goal of sending humans to Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He laid out 2030 as the date of a manned surface landing, and noted that planned 2020 Mars rover would be in support of the human mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also discussed was the use of robotics to prepare an underground habitat for the arriving people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He noted the advantages of living underground on Mars, especially that it eliminates the need to construct above ground shielding.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Top surface activity was not excluded however, just that the crew would "probably live underground for the most part".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Living underground on Mars offered many advantages in regards to human survivability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The underground base would be prepared in advance by an armada of robots, robotic precursors to human presence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Interplanetary_Transport_System_(2016)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Interplanetary_Transport_System_.282016.29">\n        Interplanetary Transport System (2016)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Interplanetary Transport System (2016)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interplanetary_Transport_System" title="Interplanetary Transport System">\n        Interplanetary Transport System\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In September 2016,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       publicly announced a comprehensive vision to begin the colonization of Mars called\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interplanetary_Transport_System" title="Interplanetary Transport System">\n        Interplanetary Transport System\n       </a>\n       (formerly, Mars Colonial Transporter), including a number of high-level design details for an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ITS_launch_vehicle" title="ITS launch vehicle">\n        ITS launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interplanetary_Spaceship" title="Interplanetary Spaceship">\n         Interplanetary Spaceship\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ITS_tanker" title="ITS tanker">\n         ITS tanker\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       spacecraft that would provide the on-orbit pieces of the transportation technology, as well as a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SpaceX_Mars_propellant_plant" title="SpaceX Mars propellant plant">\n        propellant plant to be built on Mars\n       </a>\n       , at a base referred to as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Base_Alpha" title="Mars Base Alpha">\n        Mars Base Alpha\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gw20161023_92-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gw20161023-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The aspirational objective is to advance the technology and infrastructure such that the first humans to Mars could potentially depart as early as 2024.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20161010_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20161010-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfi20160927_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfi20160927-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20160927_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20160927-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musk.40smuHK20160126_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-musk.40smuHK20160126-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Mars_Base_Camp_(2016)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_Base_Camp_.282016.29">\n        Mars Base Camp (2016)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Mars Base Camp (2016)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Base_Camp" title="Mars Base Camp">\n        Mars Base Camp\n       </a>\n       (MBC), an American spacecraft concept that proposes to send astronauts to Mars as early as 2028. The vehicle design, developed by Lockheed Martin,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars-base-camp_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-base-camp-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       would utilize both future and heritage concepts as well as the Orion MPCV built by NASA.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Deep_Space_Transport_(2017)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Deep_Space_Transport_.282017.29">\n        Deep Space Transport (2017)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Deep Space Transport (2017)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deep_Space_Transport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="695" data-file-width="937" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Deep_Space_Transport.jpg/220px-Deep_Space_Transport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Deep_Space_Transport.jpg/330px-Deep_Space_Transport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Deep_Space_Transport.jpg/440px-Deep_Space_Transport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deep_Space_Transport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Deep Space Transport\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Transport" title="Deep Space Transport">\n        Deep Space Transport\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Deep Space Transport (DST) is a spacecraft meant to be launched on top of NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        SLS\n       </a>\n       launch vehicle in 2027. It was announced by NASA in March 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Plans at present predict it to dock with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Gateway" title="Deep Space Gateway">\n        Deep Space Gateway\n       </a>\n       (DSG) station, which would be in cis-lunar space after its construction from 2021 to 2026 as a manned lunar space station, the first of its kind, in 2027. Current plans show it to be sent with a crew of 4 to Mars in 2033. It would not, however, land, but merely remain in Martian orbit until there is a launch window for a return. The mission is expected to take about 2 years if all missions in the DSG and DST from 2021-2030 are successful. This mission would use only the SLS rocket for launches, with the Orion MPCV to be used as a spacecraft to transport the crew to and from the Earth and the DSG and DST.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_intentions_by_nations_and_space_agencies">\n        Current intentions by nations and space agencies\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Current intentions by nations and space agencies">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="829" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg/220px-ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg/330px-ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg/440px-ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS-Derived_Deep_Space_Habitat_with_CPS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist\'s rendering of the planned Orion/DSH/Cryogenic Propulsion Module assembly.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A number of nations and organizations have long-term intentions to send humans to Mars.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n         United States\n        </a>\n        has a number of robotic missions currently exploring Mars, with a sample-return planned for the future. On December 5, 2014 NASA successfully launched and tested the\n        <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n         Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle\n        </a>\n        (MPCV), the first component of NASA\'s planned Mars mission program. The Orion MPCV will serve as the launch/splashdown crew delivery vehicle, in combination with a\n        <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Habitat" title="Deep Space Habitat">\n         Deep Space Habitat\n        </a>\n        module, which will provide additional living-space for the crew on the 16-month-long journey from Earth to Mars and back. The first manned Mars Mission, which will include sending astronauts to Mars, orbiting Mars, and a return to Earth, is currently scheduled for the 2030s.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n         <a href="#cite_note-103">\n          [103]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n         <a href="#cite_note-104">\n          [104]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n         <a href="#cite_note-105">\n          [105]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Technology development to facilitate US government missions to Mars is underway, but the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obama_administration" title="Obama administration">\n         Obama administration\n        </a>\n        , like several presidential administrations before, has not left a well-funded approach to actually bring the conceptual project to completion with human landings on Mars by the mid-2030s, the stated objective.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars20161012_106-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ars20161012-106">\n          [106]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        NASA is currently under presidential orders to land humans on Mars by 2033, and NASA-funded engineers have discovered a way to build potential human habitats on that planet by producing bricks from pressurized Martian soil, with the\n        <a href="/wiki/Iron_oxide" title="Iron oxide">\n         iron oxide\n        </a>\n        in the soil functioning as a binding agent.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n         <a href="#cite_note-107">\n          [107]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n         European Space Agency\n        </a>\n        has a long-term goal to send humans but has not yet built a manned spacecraft. It has sent robotic probes like\n        <a href="/wiki/ExoMars" title="ExoMars">\n         ExoMars\n        </a>\n        in 2016 and plans to send the next probe in 2020.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_(201503120102HQ).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2844" data-file-width="3939" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg/220px-Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg/330px-Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg/440px-Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_%28201503120102HQ%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Expedition_42_Soyuz_TMA-14M_Landing_(201503120102HQ).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Soyuz landing on Earth in 2015\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">\n         India\n        </a>\n        successfully placed an unmanned\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission" title="Mars Orbiter Mission">\n         Mars Orbiter Mission\n        </a>\n        (also called\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangalyaan" title="Mangalyaan">\n         Mangalyaan\n        </a>\n        ) satellite in Mars orbit on 23 September 2014.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n         <a href="#cite_note-108">\n          [108]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">\n         ISRO\n        </a>\n        plans to develop and launch a follow-up mission called\n        <a href="/wiki/Mangalyaan_2" title="Mangalyaan 2">\n         <i>\n          Mangalyaan\n         </i>\n         2\n        </a>\n        with a greater scientific payload to Mars between 2018 and 2020.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econtimes20141112_109-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-econtimes20141112-109">\n          [109]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n         <a href="#cite_note-110">\n          [110]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This mission will likely consist of a\n        <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">\n         lander\n        </a>\n        and a\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars_rover" title="Mars rover">\n         Mars rover\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibn20141030_111-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ibn20141030-111">\n          [111]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n         <a href="#cite_note-112">\n          [112]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        No plans for an Indian human mission to Mars have been made public.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">\n         Japan\n        </a>\n        has sent one robotic mission to Mars in 1998, the\n        <a href="/wiki/Nozomi_(spacecraft)" title="Nozomi (spacecraft)">\n         Nozomi\n        </a>\n        , but it failed to achieve Mars orbit.\n        <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">\n         JAXA\n        </a>\n        has proposed a rover mission called\n        <a href="/wiki/MELOS" title="MELOS">\n         MELOS\n        </a>\n        for an engineering demonstration of precision landing, and to look for possible biosignatures on Mars in 2020 or 2022. No plans for a Japanese human mission to Mars have been made public.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Government_of_China" title="Government of China">\n         China\n        </a>\n        \'s first attempted mission to Mars, the\n        <a href="/wiki/Yinghuo-1" title="Yinghuo-1">\n         Yinghuo-1\n        </a>\n        space probe, was lost with Russia\'s sample return mission to\n        <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">\n         Phobos\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">\n         Fobos-Grunt\n        </a>\n        in 2011-2012. China plans to develop and launch an orbiter, lander and rover to\n        <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n         Mars\n        </a>\n        in July or August 2020\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters20160824_113-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-reuters20160824-113">\n          [113]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n         <a href="#cite_note-114">\n          [114]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        with a\n        <a href="/wiki/Long_March_5" title="Long March 5">\n         Long March 5\n        </a>\n        heavy lift rocket.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_2015_115-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Jones_2015-115">\n          [115]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n         <a href="#cite_note-116">\n          [116]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n         <a href="#cite_note-117">\n          [117]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        A crewed phase is planned for the 2040-2060 timeframe.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n         <a href="#cite_note-118">\n          [118]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">\n         Russia\n        </a>\n        plans to send humans in the 2040-2045 timeframe.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n         <a href="#cite_note-119">\n          [119]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Technological_innovations_and_hurdles">\n        Technological innovations and hurdles\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Technological innovations and hurdles">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="5760" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg/220px-Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg/330px-Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg/440px-Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Food_Production_-_Bisected.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Depiction of plants growing in a Mars base. NASA plans to grow plants in space to help feed astronauts, in support of pioneering space.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n          <a href="#cite_note-120">\n           [120]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robonaut_2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Robonaut_2.jpg/220px-Robonaut_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Robonaut_2.jpg/330px-Robonaut_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Robonaut_2.jpg/440px-Robonaut_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robonaut_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NASA has stated that robots will prepare an underground base for a human surface mission.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolden_91-7">\n          <a href="#cite_note-bolden-91">\n           [91]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Significant technological hurdles need to be overcome for human spaceflight to Mars.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Entry into the thin and shallow Martian atmosphere will pose significant difficulties with re-entry and for a spacecraft of the weight needed to carry humans, along with life support, supplies and other equipment. Should a heat shield be used, it would need to be very large. Retro rockets could be used, but would add significant further weight.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A return mission to Mars will need to land a rocket to carry crew off the surface. Launch requirements mean that this rocket would be significantly smaller than an Earth-to-orbit rocket. Mars-to-orbit launch can also be achieved in single stage. Despite this, landing an ascent rocket on Mars will be difficult. Reentry for a large rocket will be difficult.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       One of the medical supplies that may be needed is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intravenous_fluid" title="Intravenous fluid">\n        intravenous fluid\n       </a>\n       , which is mostly water but contains other things so it can be added directly to the human blood stream. If it can be created on the spot from existing water then it could spare the weight of hauling earth-produced units, whose weight is mostly water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ivegen_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ivegen-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A prototype for this capability was tested on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ivegen_121-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ivegen-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While it is possible for humans to breathe pure oxygen, a pure oxygen atmosphere was implicated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">\n        Apollo 1\n       </a>\n       fire. As such, Mars habitats may have a need for additional gases. One possibility is to take\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Argon" title="Argon">\n        argon\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">\n        atmosphere of Mars\n       </a>\n       ; however, they are hard to separate from each other.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gas_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gas-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As a result, a Mars habitat may use 40% argon, 40% nitrogen, and 20% oxygen.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gas_122-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gas-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another concept for breathing air is to use re-usable amine bead carbon dioxide scrubbers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spectrum.ieee.org_123-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spectrum.ieee.org-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While one carbon dioxide scrubber filters the astronaut\'s air, the other is vented to the Mars atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spectrum.ieee.org_123-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spectrum.ieee.org-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Precursor_missions">\n        Precursor missions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Precursor missions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Some missions may be considered a "Mission to Mars" in their own right, or they may only be one step in a more in-depth program. An example of this is missions to Mars\' moons, or flyby missions.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Manned_flyby">\n        Manned flyby\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Manned flyby">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       An example of this is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inspiration_Mars" title="Inspiration Mars">\n        Inspiration Mars\n       </a>\n       , which could be compared to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Manned_Venus_Flyby" title="Manned Venus Flyby">\n        Manned Venus Flyby\n       </a>\n       (NASA) mission proposal of the 1970s, but for Mars.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Missions_to_Deimos_or_Phobos">\n        Missions to Deimos or Phobos\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Missions to Deimos or Phobos">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Many Mars mission concepts propose precursor missions to the moons of Mars, for example, a sample return mission to the Mars moon Phobos\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-authors.library.caltech.edu_124-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-authors.library.caltech.edu-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 not quite Mars, but perhaps a convenient stepping stone to an eventual Martian surface mission. Lockheed Martin, as part of their "Stepping stones to Mars" project, called the "Red Rocks Project", proposed to explore Mars robotically from Deimos.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footstepstomars_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-footstepstomars-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Use of fuel produced from water resources on Phobos or Deimos has also been proposed.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_sample_return_missions">\n        Mars sample return missions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Mars sample return missions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scim_br.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="252" data-file-width="252" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Scim_br.jpg/220px-Scim_br.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Scim_br.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scim_br.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist concept of SCIM passing through the Martian atmosphere. This was a simpler sample return architecture that achieved being one of four semi-finalists in the 2002 Mars Scout selection. That mission slot was ultimately won by the Phoenix lander\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="996" data-file-width="960" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg/220px-Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg/330px-Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg/440px-Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_sample_returnjpl.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sample return mission concept\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       An unmanned\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_sample_return_mission" title="Mars sample return mission">\n        Mars sample return mission\n       </a>\n       (MSR) has sometimes been considered to be an essential precursor to crewed missions to Mars\' surface by the 21st century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa.int_127-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-esa.int-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ESA noted that a sample return as being essential and could bridge the gap between robotic and human missions to Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa.int_127-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-esa.int-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An example of a Mars sample return mission is\n       <a href="/wiki/Sample_Collection_for_Investigation_of_Mars" title="Sample Collection for Investigation of Mars">\n        Sample Collection for Investigation of Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USRA-2008_128-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USRA-2008-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Mars sample return was the highest priority Flagship Mission proposed for NASA by the\n       <i>\n        Planetary Decadal Survey 2013-2022: The Future of Planetary Science\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, such missions have been hampered by complexity and expense, with one ESA proposal involving no less than five different unmanned spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return_130-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A difficulty in sample return plans is the concern that, however remote, something could be brought back that could infect life on the Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return_130-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Regardless, a basic set of guidelines for extraterrestrial sample return have been laid out depending on the source of sample (e.g. asteroid, Moon, Mars surface, etc.)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congrexprojects.com_131-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-congrexprojects.com-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hardware and mission parameters are designed following\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_protection" title="Planetary protection">\n        planetary protection\n       </a>\n       protocols so mission concepts can proceed forward in an orderly way without causing undue concern over remote chances.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congrexprojects.com_131-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-congrexprojects.com-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The issue of sample protection is another factor that increases the difficulty of sample return, both to keep the sample from getting contaminated with Earth material or life, and achieving a rational approach to keeping the Mars sample from "contaminating" Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return_130-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESA_-_Mars_Sample_Return-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the dawn of the 21st century, NASA crafted four potential pathways to Mars human missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marsd_132-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-marsd-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Of those four, three included a Mars sample return as a prerequisite to human landing, however one did not.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marsd_132-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-marsd-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crewed_orbital_missions">\n        Crewed orbital missions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Crewed orbital missions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_A._Landis" title="Geoffrey A. Landis">\n        Landis\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Lupisella proposed to explore Mars via\n       <a href="/wiki/Telepresence" title="Telepresence">\n        telepresence\n       </a>\n       from human astronauts in orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lupisella_134-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lupisella-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A similar idea, was the proposed "Human Exploration using Real-time Robotic Operations" (HERRO) mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another proposed mission was the Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Piloted_Orbital_Station" title="Mars Piloted Orbital Station">\n        Mars Piloted Orbital Station\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_mission_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n If an astronaut becomes contaminated or infected, it is conceivable that he or she could transmit Martian biological entities or even disease to fellow astronauts, or introduce such entities into the biosphere upon returning to Earth.
